class="mw-body-content"><!-- CentralNotice --></div><div class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n<div id="mw-indicator-featured-star" class="mw-indicator"><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Featured_lists" title="This is a featured list. srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/30px-Cscr-featured.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e7/Cscr-featured.svg/40px-Cscr-featured.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="462" data-file-height="438" /></a></div>\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">List of women cabinet ministers of the Republic of Ireland</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:20111203191857_M%C3%A1ire_Geoghegan-Quinn_International_Year_of_Chemistry_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="M\xc3\xa1ire Geoghegan-Quinn." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/20111203191857_M%C3%A1ire_Geoghegan-Quinn_International_Year_of_Chemistry_%28cropped%29.jpg/170px-20111203191857_M%C3%A1ire_Geoghegan-Quinn_International_Year_of_Chemistry_%28cropped%29.jpg" width="170" height="227" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/20111203191857_M%C3%A1ire_Geoghegan-Quinn_International_Year_of_Chemistry_%28cropped%29.jpg/255px-20111203191857_M%C3%A1ire_Geoghegan-Quinn_International_Year_of_Chemistry_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/20111203191857_M%C3%A1ire_Geoghegan-Quinn_International_Year_of_Chemistry_%28cropped%29.jpg/340px-20111203191857_M%C3%A1ire_Geoghegan-Quinn_International_Year_of_Chemistry_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="576" data-file-height="768" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:20111203191857_M%C3%A1ire_Geoghegan-Quinn_International_Year_of_Chemistry_(cropped).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1ire_Geoghegan-Quinn" title="M\xc3\xa1ire Geoghegan-Quinn">M\xc3\xa1ire Geoghegan-Quinn</a>, who in 1979 became the first woman in an Irish cabinet since 1921</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Ireland" title="Government of Ireland">Government of Ireland</a> (<a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">Irish</a>: <i lang="ga">Rialtas na h\xc3\x89ireann</i>) is the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">cabinet</a> that exercises executive authority in the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a>. Its ministers are collectively responsible for the Departments of State administered by the members of the Government.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>As of  October&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_women_cabinet_ministers_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, nineteen women have served as cabinet ministers in governments of the Republic of Ireland and its predecessors the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a> (1922\xe2\x80\x931937) and the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Republic" title="Irish Republic">Irish Republic</a> (1919\xe2\x80\x931922).<sup id="cite_ref-i-indep-2017-12-03_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-i-indep-2017-12-03-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> \nAfter a 58-year gap between the first and second women ministers,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200018_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200018-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> there has been at least one woman in all cabinets since December 1982. No woman has ever been <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> (prime minister), but four women have served as <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A1naiste" title="T\xc3\xa1naiste">T\xc3\xa1naiste</a> (deputy prime minister).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> Other women have served outside the cabinet as junior ministers, known until 1978 as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Parliamentary_Secretaries_of_Ireland" title="List of Parliamentary Secretaries of Ireland">Parliamentary Secretaries</a>, and since then as <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_(Ireland)" title="Minister of State (Ireland)">Ministers of State</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;n 1&#93;</a></sup> For example, three of the nineteen Ministers of State appointed In June 2017 were women.<sup id="cite_ref-irishtimes-2017-06-21-only3_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irishtimes-2017-06-21-only3-9">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_32nd_D%C3%A1il#31st_Government_of_Ireland" title="Government of the 32nd D\xc3\xa1il">31st Government of Ireland</a> was formed in June 2017. As of  October&#160;2018<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_women_cabinet_ministers_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> it includes four women as ministers in the cabinet of Taoiseach <a href="/wiki/Leo_Varadkar" title="Leo Varadkar">Leo Varadkar</a>: <a href="/wiki/Heather_Humphreys" title="Heather Humphreys">Heather Humphreys</a>, <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Zappone" title="Katherine Zappone">Katherine Zappone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regina_Doherty" title="Regina Doherty">Regina Doherty</a> and <a href="/wiki/Josepha_Madigan" title="Josepha Madigan">Josepha Madigan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DTaoiseach-current-ministers_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTaoiseach-current-ministers-10">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>  No more than four women have served simultaneously in any cabinet, and a 2014 pledge by the then-Taoiseach <a href="/wiki/Enda_Kenny" title="Enda Kenny">Enda Kenny</a> to create a gender-balanced cabinet remains unfulfilled.<sup id="cite_ref-itimes-kenny-50-50-women-2014_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itimes-kenny-50-50-women-2014-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-thejournal-2016-no-increase_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thejournal-2016-no-increase-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Criticism of the imbalance is defended by pointing to male dominance of the <a href="/wiki/Oireachtas" title="Oireachtas">Oireachtas</a> (parliament) from which ministers are appointed.<sup id="cite_ref-i-indep=2017-06-17_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-i-indep=2017-06-17-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#Constitution"><span class="tocnumber">1</span> <span class="toctext">Constitution</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-2"><a href="#History"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">History</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Calls_for_gender_balance"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Calls for gender balance</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-4"><a href="#List_of_women_ministers"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">List of women ministers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Timeline"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Timeline</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Number_of_women_ministers_in_each_Cabinet"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Number of women ministers in each Cabinet</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Notes"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Notes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitution">Constitution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_women_cabinet_ministers_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Constitution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin-Dept-Of-Taoiseach-2012.JPG" class="image"><img alt="Government Buildings, Dublin." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Dublin-Dept-Of-Taoiseach-2012.JPG/220px-Dublin-Dept-Of-Taoiseach-2012.JPG" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Dublin-Dept-Of-Taoiseach-2012.JPG/330px-Dublin-Dept-Of-Taoiseach-2012.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Dublin-Dept-Of-Taoiseach-2012.JPG/440px-Dublin-Dept-Of-Taoiseach-2012.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4524" data-file-height="3363" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dublin-Dept-Of-Taoiseach-2012.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Government_Buildings" title="Government Buildings">Government Buildings</a> in Dublin, where the Irish cabinet has met since 1922.</div></div></div>\n<p>The 1937 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">Constitution of Ireland</a> requires the government to consist of between seven and fifteen members,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> including the <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> (prime minister). The Taoiseach is elected by <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann" title="D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann">D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</a> (the lower house of the Oireachtas),<sup id="cite_ref-constitution-13.1_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-13.1-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> and chooses the other ministers<sup id="cite_ref-constitution-13.1_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-13.1-15">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> including the <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A1naiste" title="T\xc3\xa1naiste">T\xc3\xa1naiste</a> (deputy prime minister).<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_18th_D%C3%A1il#12th_Government_of_Ireland" title="Government of the 18th D\xc3\xa1il">12th Government of Ireland</a> in 1966,<sup id="cite_ref-DTaoiseach-18th-Dail_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTaoiseach-18th-Dail-17">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> all Irish cabinets have been formed with the constitutional maximum of fifteen ministers.  The total sometimes falls below this number for brief periods following the resignation of individual ministers or the withdrawal of a party from a coalition. For example, six ministers resigned in January 2011 from the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_30th_D%C3%A1il#28th_Government_of_Ireland" title="Government of the 30th D\xc3\xa1il">28th Government of Ireland</a>, and were not replaced until March, when the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_31st_D%C3%A1il" title="Government of the 31st D\xc3\xa1il">29th Government</a> was formed after the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_2011" title="Irish general election, 2011">general election in February</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-independent-worstweek_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-independent-worstweek-18">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DTaoiseach-30th-Dail_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTaoiseach-30th-Dail-19">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-rte-2011-01-20-election-date_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rte-2011-01-20-election-date-20">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Each minister must be a member of the <a href="/wiki/Oireachtas" title="Oireachtas">Oireachtas</a> (the national parliament),<sup id="cite_ref-ministers-dail-seanad_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ministers-dail-seanad-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> whose eligibility criteria for membership are defined as being "without distinction of sex".<sup id="cite_ref-oireachtas-members-sex_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oireachtas-members-sex-22">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>  Up to two members of the Government may be members of <a href="/wiki/Seanad_%C3%89ireann" title="Seanad \xc3\x89ireann">Seanad \xc3\x89ireann</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Upper_house" title="Upper house">upper house</a> of the Oireachtas,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> but the only three senators ever appointed as ministers were men.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEO&#39;TooleDooney20099_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEO&#39;TooleDooney20099-24">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>  All women in Irish cabinets have been <a href="/wiki/Teachta_D%C3%A1la" title="Teachta D\xc3\xa1la">Teachta\xc3\xad D\xc3\xa1la</a> (TDs), i.e. members of D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_women_cabinet_ministers_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Countess_Markiewicz.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Constance Markievicz." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/46/Countess_Markiewicz.jpg/170px-Countess_Markiewicz.jpg" width="170" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/46/Countess_Markiewicz.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="250" data-file-height="349" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Countess_Markiewicz.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Constance_Markievicz" title="Constance Markievicz">Constance Markievicz</a>, the first woman cabinet minister in Ireland</div></div></div>\n<p>The first woman cabinet minister in Ireland was <a href="/wiki/Constance_Markievicz" title="Constance Markievicz">Constance Markievicz</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200074_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200074-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> who in April 1919 became <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Labour" title="Minister for Labour">Minister for Labour</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_1st_D%C3%A1il#2nd_Ministry" title="Government of the 1st D\xc3\xa1il">Second Ministry</a> of the revolutionary <a href="/wiki/First_D%C3%A1il" title="First D\xc3\xa1il">First D\xc3\xa1il</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DTaoiseach-1st-Dail_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTaoiseach-1st-Dail-26">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> She was only<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEColeman201347_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEColeman201347-27">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-i-indep-2015-12-13-mgq_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-i-indep-2015-12-13-mgq-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> the second woman minister in the national government of any country, after <a href="/wiki/Alexandra_Kollontai" title="Alexandra Kollontai">Alexandra Kollontai</a>\'s appointment in 1917 as <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Commissar" class="mw-redirect" title="People&#39;s Commissar">People\'s Commissar</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Soviet_Federative_Socialist_Republic" title="Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic">Russian Soviet Federative Socialist Republic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEOffen2000341_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEOffen2000341-29">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When the <a href="/wiki/Second_D%C3%A1il" title="Second D\xc3\xa1il">Second D\xc3\xa1il</a> assembled in August 1921, Markievicz continued as Minister for Labour,<sup id="cite_ref-DTaoiseach-2nd-Dail_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTaoiseach-2nd-Dail-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> but her post was no longer at cabinet level in the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_2nd_D%C3%A1il" title="Government of the 2nd D\xc3\xa1il">Government of the Second D\xc3\xa1il</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200074_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200074-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Markievicz and other ministers opposed to the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish_Treaty" title="Anglo-Irish Treaty">Anglo-Irish Treaty</a> resigned from the Government on 9 January 1922.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200074_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200074-25">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-DTaoiseach-2nd-Dail_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTaoiseach-2nd-Dail-30">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_1922" title="Irish general election, 1922">general election in June 1922</a> saw only two women returned to the <a href="/wiki/Third_D%C3%A1il" title="Third D\xc3\xa1il">Third D\xc3\xa1il</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200083_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200083-31">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> down from six at the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_1921" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish general election, 1921">1921 election</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200075_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200075-32">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> when 4.7% of TDs were women. The 1920s and 1930s were a conservative period in Ireland, in which women\'s rights were reversed,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200016_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200016-33">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and no women were members of the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_of_the_Irish_Free_State" title="Executive Council of the Irish Free State">Executive Council</a> of the 1922\xe2\x80\x931937 <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a>. From the 1930s to the 1960s most women TDs were widows or other relatives of deceased TDs,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200016,_64_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200016,_64-34">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> and the 4.7% ratio achieved in 1921 was <a href="/wiki/List_of_women_in_D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann#Number_of_women_elected_in_each_D\xc3\xa1il" title="List of women in D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann">not equalled again</a> until the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_1981" title="Irish general election, 1981">1981 general election</a> returned 11 women, who comprised 6.6% of the <a href="/wiki/Members_of_the_22nd_D%C3%A1il" title="Members of the 22nd D\xc3\xa1il">22nd D\xc3\xa1il</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney2000115_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney2000115-35">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Niamh_Bhreathnach.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Niamh Bhreathnach." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Niamh_Bhreathnach.jpg/170px-Niamh_Bhreathnach.jpg" width="170" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/85/Niamh_Bhreathnach.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="223" data-file-height="279" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Niamh_Bhreathnach.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Niamh_Bhreathnach" title="Niamh Bhreathnach">Niamh Bhreathnach</a>, the first woman to be appointed as minister at the start of her first D\xc3\xa1il term</div></div></div>\n<p>More than 58 years elapsed between Markievicz leaving office and the appointment in December 1979 of <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1ire_Geoghegan-Quinn" title="M\xc3\xa1ire Geoghegan-Quinn">M\xc3\xa1ire Geoghegan-Quinn</a> as the second woman in cabinet.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200018_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200018-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>  In 1977, Geoghegan-Quinn had become the first woman since Markievicz to serve as a junior minister in the Irish government,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017Box_9.1_Firsts_for_women_in_politics_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017Box_9.1_Firsts_for_women_in_politics-36">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> when <a href="/wiki/Jack_Lynch" title="Jack Lynch">Jack Lynch</a> appointed her as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Parliamentary_Secretaries_of_Ireland#Parliamentary_Secretary_to_the_Minister_for_Industry_and_Commerce" title="List of Parliamentary Secretaries of Ireland">Parliamentary Secretary to the Minister for Industry and Commerce</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DTaoiseach-21st-Dail_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTaoiseach-21st-Dail-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>  Two years later, aged 29, she was "flabbergasted"<sup id="cite_ref-i-indep-2015-12-13-mgq_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-i-indep-2015-12-13-mgq-28">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> to become <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_the_Gaeltacht" class="mw-redirect" title="Minister for the Gaeltacht">Minister for the Gaeltacht</a> in the first cabinet of Taoiseach <a href="/wiki/Charles_Haughey" title="Charles Haughey">Charles Haughey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DTaoiseach-21st-Dail_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTaoiseach-21st-Dail-37">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since then, the only all-male Irish government was the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_23rd_D%C3%A1il" title="Government of the 23rd D\xc3\xa1il">March\xe2\x80\x93December 1982 second government of Charles Haughey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DTaoiseach-23rd-Dail_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTaoiseach-23rd-Dail-38">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> All cabinets since December 1982 have included at least one woman. The first time two women served as ministers simultaneously was in January 1993, when Taoiseach <a href="/wiki/Albert_Reynolds" title="Albert Reynolds">Albert Reynolds</a> included both M\xc3\xa1ire Geoghegan-Quinn and <a href="/wiki/Niamh_Bhreathnach" title="Niamh Bhreathnach">Niamh Bhreathnach</a> in <a href="/wiki/23rd_Government_of_Ireland" title="23rd Government of Ireland">his cabinet</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DTaoiseach-27th-Dail_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTaoiseach-27th-Dail-39">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Bhreathnach was the first woman to be appointed as minister at the start of her first D\xc3\xa1il term,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney2000139_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney2000139-40">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> and the only one until <a href="/wiki/Katherine_Zappone" title="Katherine Zappone">Katherine Zappone</a> became <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Children_and_Youth_Affairs" title="Minister for Children and Youth Affairs">Minister for Children and Youth Affairs</a> in May 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mary_Harney_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Mary Harney." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Mary_Harney_cropped.jpg/170px-Mary_Harney_cropped.jpg" width="170" height="206" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ec/Mary_Harney_cropped.jpg/255px-Mary_Harney_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/ec/Mary_Harney_cropped.jpg 2x" data-file-width="316" data-file-height="383" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mary_Harney_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mary_Harney" title="Mary Harney">Mary Harney</a>, the first woman <a href="/wiki/T%C3%A1naiste" title="T\xc3\xa1naiste">T\xc3\xa1naiste</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Only three ministerial offices are specifically identified in the constitution: Taoiseach, T\xc3\xa1naiste and <a href="/wiki/Minister_for_Finance_(Ireland)" title="Minister for Finance (Ireland)">Minister for Finance</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ministers-dail-seanad_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ministers-dail-seanad-21">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>  No woman has ever been elected as Taoiseach<sup id="cite_ref-former-taoisigh_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-former-taoisigh-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> or appointed as Minister for Finance.<sup id="cite_ref-finance-ministers_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finance-ministers-42">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> However, four women have served as T\xc3\xa1naiste.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The first woman T\xc3\xa1naiste was <a href="/wiki/Mary_Harney" title="Mary Harney">Mary Harney</a> (1997\xe2\x80\x932006), who in 1993 had become the first woman to lead a political party in the D\xc3\xa1il.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney2000121_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney2000121-43">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Harney was followed by <a href="/wiki/Mary_Coughlan_(politician)" title="Mary Coughlan (politician)">Mary Coughlan</a> (2008\xe2\x80\x932011),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017_4-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Joan_Burton" title="Joan Burton">Joan Burton</a> (2014\xe2\x80\x932016),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Frances_Fitzgerald_(politician)" title="Frances Fitzgerald (politician)">Frances Fitzgerald</a> (2016\xe2\x80\x932017).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Political scientists Yvonne Galligan and Fiona Buckley note that women have been grossly under-represented in Irish politics,<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> with men making up 91% of all cabinet appointments between 1919 and June 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017_4-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> They also found that women in the Irish cabinet are twice as likely to hold a social portfolio (48%) than an economic portfolio (24%).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017_4-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> By contrast, only 17% of men held social portfolios, and 52% held an economic or foreign affairs portfolio.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017_4-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGalliganBuckley2017-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>All but two of the women who have served as ministers since 1919 are still alive. The first Irish woman minister, Constance Markievicz, died in 1927,<sup id="cite_ref-oireachtas-db-constance-markievicz_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oireachtas-db-constance-markievicz-44">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> and the third, <a href="/wiki/Eileen_Desmond" title="Eileen Desmond">Eileen Desmond</a>, died in 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-oireachtas-db-eileen-desmond_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oireachtas-db-eileen-desmond-45">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>  Ireland\'s oldest living woman former minister is <span class="currentage"></span>81-year-old<sup id="cite_ref-oireachtas-db-mary-o-rourke_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oireachtas-db-mary-o-rourke-46">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mary_O%27Rourke" title="Mary O&#39;Rourke">Mary O\'Rourke</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Calls_for_gender_balance">Calls for gender balance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_women_cabinet_ministers_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Calls for gender balance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Katherine_Zappone.png" class="image"><img alt="Katherine Zappone." src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Katherine_Zappone.png/170px-Katherine_Zappone.png" width="170" height="255" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Katherine_Zappone.png/255px-Katherine_Zappone.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Katherine_Zappone.png/340px-Katherine_Zappone.png 2x" data-file-width="1056" data-file-height="1584" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Katherine_Zappone.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Katherine_Zappone" title="Katherine Zappone">Katherine Zappone</a>, the first woman to be appointed to an Irish cabinet as an <a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">independent politician</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The highest number of women ever in an Irish cabinet is four, a number first reached in 2004\xe2\x80\x932007, and again from 2014 to the present. However, this amounts to only 27% of the 15 ministers, and has been criticised by the <a href="/wiki/National_Women%27s_Council_of_Ireland" title="National Women&#39;s Council of Ireland">National Women\'s Council of Ireland</a> as "way off a gender balanced Cabinet".<sup id="cite_ref-newstalk-2017-06-15_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newstalk-2017-06-15-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, then Taoiseach <a href="/wiki/Enda_Kenny" title="Enda Kenny">Enda Kenny</a> had pledged that if re-elected he would appoint a cabinet "50:50 on merit, of men and women".<sup id="cite_ref-itimes-kenny-50-50-women-2014_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-itimes-kenny-50-50-women-2014-11">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> When Kenny formed the <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_32nd_D%C3%A1il#30th_Government_of_Ireland" title="Government of the 32nd D\xc3\xa1il">30th Government</a> in May 2016 with four women ministers, he was criticised by women campaigners for the lack of increase.<sup id="cite_ref-thejournal-2016-no-increase_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thejournal-2016-no-increase-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Minister <a href="/wiki/Regina_Doherty" title="Regina Doherty">Regina Doherty</a> defended Kenny, saying he had "probably done the best that he can do".<sup id="cite_ref-newstalk-2017-06-15_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newstalk-2017-06-15-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/TheJournal.ie" title="TheJournal.ie">TheJournal.ie</a> noted that the "proportion of senior ministers who are women is 27%, higher than the 22% of <a href="/wiki/Teachta_D%C3%A1la" title="Teachta D\xc3\xa1la">TDs</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-thejournal-2016-no-increase_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-thejournal-2016-no-increase-12">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In June 2017, Kenny\'s successor <a href="/wiki/Leo_Varadkar" title="Leo Varadkar">Leo Varadkar</a> appointed four women to his cabinet. He too was criticised for not including more women,<sup id="cite_ref-newstalk-2017-06-15_47-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newstalk-2017-06-15-47">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> but replied that "your ministerial team generally reflects the composition of the D\xc3\xa1il".<sup id="cite_ref-i-indep=2017-06-17_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-i-indep=2017-06-17-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Varadkar promised "to make sure we have many more women in our next parliamentary party so that I can promote many more women".<sup id="cite_ref-i-indep=2017-06-17_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-i-indep=2017-06-17-13">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In February 2018, Culture Minister <a href="/wiki/Josepha_Madigan" title="Josepha Madigan">Josepha Madigan</a> launched a programme of commemoration of the centenary of women\'s enfranchisement. The <a href="/wiki/Representation_of_the_People_Act_1918" title="Representation of the People Act 1918">Representation of the People Act 1918</a> gave limited voting rights for women. The right to stand for election was granted later in 1918, by the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_(Qualification_of_Women)_Act_1918" title="Parliament (Qualification of Women) Act 1918">Parliament (Qualification of Women) Act</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-iexaminer-2018-02-07_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iexaminer-2018-02-07-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200015_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMcNamaraMooney200015-49">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>   Madigan said the Irish State "failed women for far too long,"<sup id="cite_ref-irishtimes-2018-02-07_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-irishtimes-2018-02-07-50">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> and that it was time to "redouble our efforts" to provide equal opportunities.<sup id="cite_ref-iexaminer-2018-02-07_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iexaminer-2018-02-07-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> Former T\xc3\xa1naiste Joan Burton called for the next government to consist of an equal number of men and women.<sup id="cite_ref-iexaminer-2018-02-07_48-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iexaminer-2018-02-07-48">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_women_ministers">List of women ministers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_women_cabinet_ministers_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: List of women ministers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Numerical order represents the order of first appointment to the cabinet.<br />Age represents age on appointment to that office.\n</p>\n<div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:black; background-color: #cccccc; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Denotes <a href="/wiki/Incumbent" title="Incumbent">incumbent</a> minister</div>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th scope="col">#\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Name\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Portrait\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Office\n</th>\n<th colspan="2" scope="col">Party\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Appointed\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Left office\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Age\n</th>\n<th scope="col">Taoiseach\n</th>\n<th scope="col">D\xc3\xa1il\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td data-sort-value="01">1\n</td>\n<td data-sort-value="Markievicz, Constance" scope="row"><a href="/wiki/Constance_Markievicz" title="Constance Markievicz">Constance Markievicz</a><br /><span style="font-size:85%;">(1868\xe2\x80\x931927)<sup Coveney</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_women_cabinet_ministers_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-8"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-8">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Some Ministers of State, including the <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_at_the_Department_of_the_Taoiseach" title="Minister of State at the Department of the Taoiseach">Government Chief Whip</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Dtaoiseach-chief-whip_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dtaoiseach-chief-whip-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> attend cabinet meetings in a non-voting capacity, but are not members of the Government. They are formally known as "Minister of State attending Government",<sup id="cite_ref-dail-2016-05-06-members-of-government_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dail-2016-05-06-members-of-government-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> or colloquially as <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_State_(Ireland)#Super_Junior" title="Minister of State (Ireland)">"Super Junior" ministers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-rte-2017-06-20-ministers-of-state_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rte-2017-06-20-ministers-of-state-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-54"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-54">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">This column has been labelled "Taoiseach" for brevity, but it is anachronistic in the case of <a href="/wiki/Constance_Markievicz" title="Constance Markievicz">Constance Markievicz</a>\'s 1919\xe2\x80\x9321 tenure as minister. <a href="/wiki/%C3%89amon_de_Valera" title="\xc3\x89amon de Valera">\xc3\x89amon de Valera</a>\'s title as head of government in the <a href="/wiki/First_D%C3%A1il" title="First D\xc3\xa1il">First D\xc3\xa1il</a> was <i lang="ga" title="Irish language text">Pr\xc3\xadomh Aire</i>, or in English <a href="/wiki/President_of_D%C3%A1il_%C3%89ireann" title="President of D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann">President of D\xc3\xa1il \xc3\x89ireann</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-coogan-dev-president_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-coogan-dev-president-51">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> The 1922\xe2\x80\x931937 <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a>, which had no women cabinet ministers and no women <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_Secretary_(Ireland)" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary Secretary (Ireland)">Parliamentary Secretaries</a> (junior ministers), used the title <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Executive_Council_of_the_Irish_Free_State" title="President of the Executive Council of the Irish Free State">President of the Executive Council</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECoakleyGallagher2017474_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoakleyGallagher2017474-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-former-taoisigh_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-former-taoisigh-41">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> The title of <a href="/wiki/Taoiseach" title="Taoiseach">Taoiseach</a> for the head of government was introduced in the 1937 <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">Constitution of Ireland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECoakleyGallagher2017474_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoakleyGallagher2017474-52">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-constitution-28_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-28-53">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> The first woman to serve as a cabinet minister under a Taoiseach was <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A1ire_Geoghegan-Quinn" title="M\xc3\xa1ire Geoghegan-Quinn">M\xc3\xa1ire Geoghegan-Quinn</a>, who was appointed in 1979 to <a href="/wiki/Charles_Haughey" title="Charles Haughey">Charles Haughey</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Government_of_the_21st_D%C3%A1il#16th_Government_of_Ireland" title="Government of the 21st D\xc3\xa1il">first cabinet</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-harney-party-67"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-harney-party_67-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-harney-party_67-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Democrats" title="Progressive Democrats">Progressive Democrats</a> dissolved in November 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-oireachtas-db-mary-harney_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oireachtas-db-mary-harney-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Mary_Harney" title="Mary Harney">Mary Harney</a> then sat as an <a href="/wiki/Independent_politician" title="Independent politician">independent</a> TD<sup id="cite_ref-oireachtas-db-mary-harney_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oireachtas-db-mary-harney-64">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> and continued to serve as a minister for the remainder of the <a href="/wiki/30th_D%C3%A1il" class="mw-redirect" title="30th D\xc3\xa1il">30th D\xc3\xa1il</a><sup id="cite_ref-DTaoiseach-28th-Government_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DTaoiseach-28th-Government-66">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> until she retired from politics at the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_2011" title="Irish general election, 2011">2011 general election</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-simul-80"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-simul_80-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-simul_80-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">The Fourth Ministry and First Provisional Government held office simultaneously for many months.<sup id="cite_ref-mansergh-unresolved_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mansergh-unresolved-78">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The membership of both was merged when the Second Provisional Government came to office after the <a href="/wiki/Irish_general_election,_1922" title="Irish general election, 1922">1922 general election</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTECoakleyGallagher201719_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTECoakleyGallagher201719-79">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> </span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_women_cabinet_ministers_of_the_Republic_of_Ireland&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 35em; -webkit-column-width: 35em; column-width: 35em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland" title="Constitution of Ireland">Constitution of Ireland</a>, <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/Constitution_of_Ireland#THE_GOVERNMENT" class="extiw" title="s:Constitution of Ireland">Article 28, Section 4.2</a></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-i-indep-2017-12-03-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-i-indep-2017-12-03_2-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation news">McQuinn, Cormac (3 December 2017). <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.independent.ie/irish-news/politics/i-think-whats-putting-women-off-politics-is-this-hostile-environment-36373883.html">"<span class="cs1-kern-left">\'</span>I think what\'s putting women off politics is this hostile environment<span class="cs1-kern-right">\'</span>"</a>. <i><a href="/wiki/Irish_Independent" title="Irish Independent">Irish Independent</a></i>.
